An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"286cb793-86b2-4bfa-8461-7974f54fd604","uuid":"455bcc6a-529a-45a4-982d-30632b42827c","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\\\"\\n27: \\tutilruntime \\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\\\"\\n28: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\\\"\\n29: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\\\"\\n30: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\\\"\\n31: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/clock\\\"\\n32: \\n33: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n34: \\n35: \\tclientgofeaturegate \\\"k8s.io/client-go/features\\\"\\n36: )\\n37: \\n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-100\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package cache\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"errors\"\n21: \t\"fmt\"\n22: \t\"sync\"\n23: \t\"time\"\n24: \n25: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n26: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n27: \tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n28: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n29: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n30: \t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n31: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n32: \n33: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n34: \n35: \tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n36: )\n37: \n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n47: //\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n52: //\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n65: // selector.\n66: //\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n73: //\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n75: // during `Run()`.\n76: //\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\n84: //\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n91: //\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n96: // into its constituent parts.\n97: //\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-100"}}}

Note how we pass clientState in as a\n583: \t// KeyLister, that way resync operations will result in the correct set\n584: \t// of update/delete deltas.\n585: \tfifo := NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n586: \t\tKnownObjects:          clientState,\n587: \t\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true,\n588: \t\tTransformer:           options.Transform,\n589: \t})\n590: \n591: \tcfg := &Config{\n592: \t\tQueue:            fifo,\n593: \t\tListerWatcher:    options.ListerWatcher,\n594: \t\tObjectType:       options.ObjectType,\n595: \t\tFullResyncPeriod: options.ResyncPeriod,\n596: \t\tMinWatchTimeout:  options.MinWatchTimeout,\n597: \t\tRetryOnError:     false,\n598: \n599: \t\tProcess: func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error {\n600: \t\t\tif deltas, ok := obj.(Deltas); ok {\n601: \t\t\t\treturn processDeltas(options.Handler, clientState, deltas, isInInitialList)\n602: \t\t\t}\n603: \t\t\treturn errors.New(\"object given as Process argument is not Deltas\")\n604: \t\t},\n605: \t}\n606: \treturn New(cfg)\n607: }\n608: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/controller.go%3FL540-640"}}}

All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\\n36: \\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\\n37: \\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\\n38: \\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n39: \\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\\n40: \\n41: \\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\\n42: \\t// this queue \\\"knows about\\\". It is used to decide which items are missing\\n43: \\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\\n44: \\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\\n45: \\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n46: \\n47: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\\n48: \\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\\n49: \\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key. Kubernetes follows this flow:\\n\\n1. **Watch Initiation (ListWatch)**: The ListWatch type (tools/cache/listwatch.go) provides List() and Watch() methods that connect to the API server. The Watch() method returns a watch.Interface that streams events from the API server.\\n\\n2. **Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The Reflector type drives the entire flow. Its Run() method starts an infinite loop calling ListAndWatch(). The ListAndWatch() method first lists all objects, then calls watch() to set up a continuous watch stream. The watch() method calls handleWatch()/handleAnyWatch() to process events.\\n\\n3. **Processing Watch Events (reflector.go)**: handleAnyWatch() receives events from the API server via w.ResultChan() and processes them as watch.Added, watch.Modified, or watch.Deleted events. These events are immediately added to the store via store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete().\\n\\n4. **DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The store backing the Reflector is a DeltaFIFO - a queue that accumulates change deltas. Each call to Add/Update/Delete creates or appends to a Deltas object for that key. This FIFO stores deltas indexed by object key, allowing processing of all changes for an object together.\\n\\n5. **Controller Loop (tools/cache/controller.go)**: A Controller runs a loop that pops Deltas objects from the DeltaFIFO queue. Each pop call returns accumulated Deltas for a single object. The controller invokes the ProcessFunc for each popped item.\\n\\n6. **ProcessFunc and processDeltas (controller.go)**: The ProcessFunc is called with the Deltas object and delegates to processDeltas(). This function iterates through each Delta, updates the local cache (clientState), and calls the appropriate handler method (handler.OnAdd, handler.OnUpdate, or handler.OnDelete).\\n\\n7. **SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer type implements the ResourceEventHandler interface. Its OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), and OnDelete() methods receive notifications from processDeltas(). These methods update the local index cache and immediately delegate to the sharedProcessor.distribute() method.\\n\\n8. **SharedProcessor (shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor maintains a map of all registered processorListeners. Its distribute() method iterates through all listeners and calls listener.add() to queue the notification, considering whether it's a sync event or normal event.\\n\\n9. **ProcessorListener (shared_informer.go)**: Each registered ResourceEventHandler gets its own processorListener. The listener has two goroutines: pop() which transfers notifications from an unbounded ring buffer to a channel, and run() which reads from that channel and invokes the actual handler methods.\\n\\n10. **Handler Invocation (shared_informer.go)**: The processorListener.run() method reads notifications from nextCh and invokes the appropriate handler method based on notification type. For addNotification, it calls handler.OnAdd(). For updateNotification, handler.OnUpdate(). For deleteNotification, handler.OnDelete().\\n\\nThis architecture achieves several goals: (1) Multiple event handlers can register with a single informer via AddEventHandler(); (2) Events are buffered through the DeltaFIFO to handle back-pressure and accumulate changes; (3) Each handler runs in its own goroutine with its own buffer, preventing slow handlers from blocking others; (4) Events are guaranteed to be processed in order for each object; (5) Resync events can trigger re-listing all objects periodically.\\n\\nThe complete files involved are:\\n- ListWatch implementation: tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n- Watch event processing: tools/cache/reflector.go (handleAnyWatch, watch methods)\\n- Delta accumulation: tools/cache/delta_fifo.go (DeltaFIFO type)\\n- Event processing loop: tools/cache/controller.go (processDeltas function)\\n- Event distribution to handlers: tools/cache/shared_informer.go (sharedIndexInformer, sharedProcessor, processorListener)\\n- Store interface: tools/cache/store.go\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2526,"cache_read_input_tokens":86118,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2526},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"286cb793-86b2-4bfa-8461-7974f54fd604","uuid":"a084c947-4c64-4b9c-958c-984792def46b"}

Kubernetes follows this flow:\\n\\n1. **Watch Initiation (ListWatch)**: The ListWatch type (tools/cache/listwatch.go) provides List() and Watch() methods that connect to the API server. The Watch() method returns a watch.Interface that streams events from the API server.\\n\\n2. **Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The Reflector type drives the entire flow. Its Run() method starts an infinite loop calling ListAndWatch(). The ListAndWatch() method first lists all objects, then calls watch() to set up a continuous watch stream. The watch() method calls handleWatch()/handleAnyWatch() to process events.\\n\\n3. **Processing Watch Events (reflector.go)**: handleAnyWatch() receives events from the API server via w.ResultChan() and processes them as watch.Added, watch.Modified, or watch.Deleted events. These events are immediately added to the store via store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete().\\n\\n4. **DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The store backing the Reflector is a DeltaFIFO - a queue that accumulates change deltas. Each call to Add/Update/Delete creates or appends to a Deltas object for that key. This FIFO stores deltas indexed by object key, allowing processing of all changes for an object together.\\n\\n5. **Controller Loop (tools/cache/controller.go)**: A Controller runs a loop that pops Deltas objects from the DeltaFIFO queue. Each pop call returns accumulated Deltas for a single object. The controller invokes the ProcessFunc for each popped item.\\n\\n6. **ProcessFunc and processDeltas (controller.go)**: The ProcessFunc is called with the Deltas object and delegates to processDeltas(). This function iterates through each Delta, updates the local cache (clientState), and calls the appropriate handler method (handler.OnAdd, handler.OnUpdate, or handler.OnDelete).\\n\\n7. **SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer type implements the ResourceEventHandler interface. Its OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), and OnDelete() methods receive notifications from processDeltas(). These methods update the local index cache and immediately delegate to the sharedProcessor.distribute() method.\\n\\n8. **SharedProcessor (shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor maintains a map of all registered processorListeners. Its distribute() method iterates through all listeners and calls listener.add() to queue the notification, considering whether it's a sync event or normal event.\\n\\n9. **ProcessorListener (shared_informer.go)**: Each registered ResourceEventHandler gets its own processorListener. The listener has two goroutines: pop() which transfers notifications from an unbounded ring buffer to a channel, and run() which reads from that channel and invokes the actual handler methods.\\n\\n10. **Handler Invocation (shared_informer.go)**: The processorListener.run() method reads notifications from nextCh and invokes the appropriate handler method based on notification type. For addNotification, it calls handler.OnAdd(). For updateNotification, handler.OnUpdate(). For deleteNotification, handler.OnDelete().\\n\\nThis architecture achieves several goals: (1) Multiple event handlers can register with a single informer via AddEventHandler(); (2) Events are buffered through the DeltaFIFO to handle back-pressure and accumulate changes; (3) Each handler runs in its own goroutine with its own buffer, preventing slow handlers from blocking others; (4) Events are guaranteed to be processed in order for each object; (5) Resync events can trigger re-listing all objects periodically.\\n\\nThe complete files involved are:\\n- ListWatch implementation: tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n- Watch event processing: tools/cache/reflector.go (handleAnyWatch, watch methods)\\n- Delta accumulation: tools/cache/delta_fifo.go (DeltaFIFO type)\\n- Event processing loop: tools/cache/controller.go (processDeltas function)\\n- Event distribution to handlers: tools/cache/shared_informer.go (sharedIndexInformer, sharedProcessor, processorListener)\\n- Store interface: tools/cache/store.go\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

informer cache updates in Kubernetes follows this flow:\\n\\n1. **Watch Initiation (ListWatch)**: The ListWatch type (tools/cache/listwatch.go) provides List() and Watch() methods that connect to the API server. The Watch() method returns a watch.Interface that streams events from the API server.\\n\\n2. **Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The Reflector type drives the entire flow. Its Run() method starts an infinite loop calling ListAndWatch(). The ListAndWatch() method first lists all objects, then calls watch() to set up a continuous watch stream. The watch() method calls handleWatch()/handleAnyWatch() to process events.\\n\\n3. **Processing Watch Events (reflector.go)**: handleAnyWatch() receives events from the API server via w.ResultChan() and processes them as watch.Added, watch.Modified, or watch.Deleted events. These events are immediately added to the store via store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete().\\n\\n4. **DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The store backing the Reflector is a DeltaFIFO - a queue that accumulates change deltas. Each call to Add/Update/Delete creates or appends to a Deltas object for that key. This FIFO stores deltas indexed by object key, allowing processing of all changes for an object together.\\n\\n5. **Controller Loop (tools/cache/controller.go)**: A Controller runs a loop that pops Deltas objects from the DeltaFIFO queue. Each pop call returns accumulated Deltas for a single object. The controller invokes the ProcessFunc for each popped item.\\n\\n6. **ProcessFunc and processDeltas (controller.go)**: The ProcessFunc is called with the Deltas object and delegates to processDeltas(). This function iterates through each Delta, updates the local cache (clientState), and calls the appropriate handler method (handler.OnAdd, handler.OnUpdate, or handler.OnDelete).\\n\\n7. **SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer type implements the ResourceEventHandler interface. Its OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), and OnDelete() methods receive notifications from processDeltas(). These methods update the local index cache and immediately delegate to the sharedProcessor.distribute() method.\\n\\n8. **SharedProcessor (shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor maintains a map of all registered processorListeners. Its distribute() method iterates through all listeners and calls listener.add() to queue the notification, considering whether it's a sync event or normal event.\\n\\n9. **ProcessorListener (shared_informer.go)**: Each registered ResourceEventHandler gets its own processorListener. The listener has two goroutines: pop() which transfers notifications from an unbounded ring buffer to a channel, and run() which reads from that channel and invokes the actual handler methods.\\n\\n10. **Handler Invocation (shared_informer.go)**: The processorListener.run() method reads notifications from nextCh and invokes the appropriate handler method based on notification type. For addNotification, it calls handler.OnAdd(). For updateNotification, handler.OnUpdate(). For deleteNotification, handler.OnDelete().\\n\\nThis architecture achieves several goals: (1) Multiple event handlers can register with a single informer via AddEventHandler(); (2) Events are buffered through the DeltaFIFO to handle back-pressure and accumulate changes; (3) Each handler runs in its own goroutine with its own buffer, preventing slow handlers from blocking others; (4) Events are guaranteed to be processed in order for each object; (5) Resync events can trigger re-listing all objects periodically.\\n\\nThe complete files involved are:\\n- ListWatch implementation: tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n- Watch event processing: tools/cache/reflector.go (handleAnyWatch, watch methods)\\n- Delta accumulation: tools/cache/delta_fifo.go (DeltaFIFO type)\\n- Event processing loop: tools/cache/controller.go (processDeltas function)\\n- Event distribution to handlers: tools/cache/shared_informer.go (sharedIndexInformer, sharedProcessor, processorListener)\\n- Store interface: tools/cache/store.go\"\n   233→}\n   234→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \"tools/cache/shared_informer.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"processorListener.run\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The event handler chain from API server watch events to informer cache updates in Kubernetes follows this flow:\\n\\n1. **Watch Initiation (ListWatch)**: The ListWatch type (tools/cache/listwatch.go) provides List() and Watch() methods that connect to the API server. The Watch() method returns a watch.Interface that streams events from the API server.\\n\\n2. **Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The Reflector type drives the entire flow. Its Run() method starts an infinite loop calling ListAndWatch(). The ListAndWatch() method first lists all objects, then calls watch() to set up a continuous watch stream. The watch() method calls handleWatch()/handleAnyWatch() to process events.\\n\\n3. **Processing Watch Events (reflector.go)**: handleAnyWatch() receives events from the API server via w.ResultChan() and processes them as watch.Added, watch.Modified, or watch.Deleted events. These events are immediately added to the store via store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete().\\n\\n4. **DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The store backing the Reflector is a DeltaFIFO - a queue that accumulates change deltas. Each call to Add/Update/Delete creates or appends to a Deltas object for that key. This FIFO stores deltas indexed by object key, allowing processing of all changes for an object together.\\n\\n5. **Controller Loop (tools/cache/controller.go)**: A Controller runs a loop that pops Deltas objects from the DeltaFIFO queue. Each pop call returns accumulated Deltas for a single object. The controller invokes the ProcessFunc for each popped item.\\n\\n6. **ProcessFunc and processDeltas (controller.go)**: The ProcessFunc is called with the Deltas object and delegates to processDeltas(). This function iterates through each Delta, updates the local cache (clientState), and calls the appropriate handler method (handler.OnAdd, handler.OnUpdate, or handler.OnDelete).\\n\\n7. **SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer type implements the ResourceEventHandler interface. Its OnAdd(), OnUpdate(), and OnDelete() methods receive notifications from processDeltas(). These methods update the local index cache and immediately delegate to the sharedProcessor.distribute() method.\\n\\n8. **SharedProcessor (shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor maintains a map of all registered processorListeners. Its distribute() method iterates through all listeners and calls listener.add() to queue the notification, considering whether it's a sync event or normal event.\\n\\n9. **ProcessorListener (shared_informer.go)**: Each registered ResourceEventHandler gets its own processorListener. The listener has two goroutines: pop() which transfers notifications from an unbounded ring buffer to a channel, and run() which reads from that channel and invokes the actual handler methods.\\n\\n10. **Handler Invocation (shared_informer.go)**: The processorListener.run() method reads notifications from nextCh and invokes the appropriate handler method based on notification type. For addNotification, it calls handler.OnAdd(). For updateNotification, handler.OnUpdate(). For deleteNotification, handler.OnDelete().\\n\\nThis architecture achieves several goals: (1) Multiple event handlers can register with a single informer via AddEventHandler(); (2) Events are buffered through the DeltaFIFO to handle back-pressure and accumulate changes; (3) Each handler runs in its own goroutine with its own buffer, preventing slow handlers from blocking others; (4) Events are guaranteed to be processed in order for each object; (5) Resync events can trigger re-listing all objects periodically.\\n\\nThe complete files involved are:\\n- ListWatch implementation: tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n- Watch event processing: tools/cache/reflector.go (handleAnyWatch, watch methods)\\n- Delta accumulation: tools/cache/delta_fifo.go (DeltaFIFO type)\\n- Event processing loop: tools/cache/controller.go (processDeltas function)\\n- Event distribution to handlers: tools/cache/shared_informer.go (sharedIndexInformer, sharedProcessor, processorListener)\\n- Store interface: tools/cache/store.go\"\n}\n","numLines":234,"startLine":1,"totalLines":234}}}
